Prussian Prime Minister Göring Warns the People 68

Hitler Maintains Absolute Order for the Nation; The Authorities' Actions in the June 30th Incident Were Entirely Proper; Hope the Judiciary Will Follow the Leader's Will

)Berlin( Prussian Prime Minister Göring addressed a meeting of prosecutors and state lawyers today, demanding unconditional support for Chancellor Hitler and issuing warnings against judicial criticism of the government's recent actions. Göring earnestly hoped that Hitler would create absolute order in the Nazi state, defend the nation in every way, and resist all attacks. This is the responsibility of those listening to his speech today. Justice and the will of our leader are one and the same; this is the justice that the audience must uphold. Göring continued, saying that he would personally support those who fulfill their duties and severely punish those who neglect their duties. The actions of the leaders on June 30th were the highest realization of justice and the best feeling of justice. Therefore, all sectors must not allow it to be subjected to severe tests again. The clean air that the leaders' actions have already cleared should be maintained by all comrades, and they should act according to the law and the needs of the leader and the nation, without showing any favoritism. )Reuters Telegram, 12th(

(Berlin) Aviation Minister General Göring, after the recent coup, convened the prosecutors of the Prussian provinces. Before the Central Minister of Justice Gürtner and the Chief of Secret Police Himmler, he clarified the concept of law, saying, "National Socialism can only have one concept of law, that is, the concept determined by Chancellor Hitler himself." Göring also said that Hitler wanted everyone in the National Socialist state to absolutely abide by discipline, and all prosecutors should protect the state in their duties and severely punish those who attack the state and Chancellor Hitler. After the incident of June 30th, when the Chancellor quelled the rebellion, people felt uneasy, but now normalcy has been restored. Some advocates of extreme legalism say that everything can be destroyed, but the law must be maintained. We cannot agree with this. We National Socialists believe that the people are the beginning of everything, and the law is made by the people themselves. The Chancellor has said that in a country, the law and the will of the people are exactly the same. Therefore, no one can give the law the nature of an enemy state. Göring continued that the June 30th incident relieved Germany of its greatest danger. The reason why it was able to do so was due to the swift actions of Hitler and his representatives. He said, "The actions of the National Socialist authorities in these days are a manifestation of the conscience and law of the German people. Therefore, this action is entirely proper. No one has the right to review it afterward. This action is also extremely clean. No one has the right to oppose the Chancellor for personal reasons, soiling his clean action. Anyone who opposes it, no matter who they are, will be severely punished. Those who fabricate rumors should also be severely punished. In short, there is only one concept of law, that is, the concept determined by the Chancellor." )Havas Telegram, 12th(

Johnson Mourns and Speaks of America's Waterloo 69

US Aircraft Squadron's Flight to Alaska Delayed Due to Dock Workers' Strike 75

(Washington) The grand squadron flight originally scheduled by the War Department to fly to Alaska in early July has been learned today that it has been postponed to late this month. A Chapter in Japanese-Russian War History: Piłsudski Solicits Japan for Poland's Independence 76

Marshal Józef Piłsudski, the current Polish Minister of National Defense, is a founding father of Poland. He had a connection with Japan thirty years ago during the Russo-Japanese War. The following is a narrative: At that time, Piłsudski was a member of a secret political organization, engaging in disturbances within the territory of the old Russian Empire, seeking independence for Poland. However, due to the unfavorable situation, he had to leave the Russian border. Piłsudski had a friend named Filipowicz, who later served as the Polish Ambassador to the United States, and was then a fellow socialist fighter with Piłsudski. He was on good terms with the Japanese. Piłsudski was introduced by him and became acquainted with Utsunomiya, the military attaché at the Japanese Embassy in London. Utsunomiya then invited Piłsudski and Filipowicz to visit Japan. Piłsudski originally intended to provide Japan with information about the Russian army in exchange for obtaining Japanese military equipment and ammunition to assist the Polish Independence Party, so he made the trip to Japan. He landed in Yokohama on July 10, 1904, when the Russo-Japanese War was in full swing, exactly thirty years ago. Later, in Tokyo, Piłsudski met with Japanese Generals Murata and Inoue Toshio. Inoue Toshio was the first Japanese Minister to Poland after Poland's founding. Piłsudski's meeting with the two was quite harmonious, but there were no concrete results. When Piłsudski was about to return to his country, a few days before his departure, Japanese General Inagaki told him, "The Japanese government is probably unwilling to take any action politically for Poland. Japanese soldiers are very willing to have relations with the Polish independence movement." After this remark, Japanese officers in Switzerland soon trained Polish people with military technical knowledge. Therefore, when Piłsudski left Japan to return to his country, he not only had no resentment, but also had some gratitude. )Havas Telegram, 12th(

Japan's Explanation to Britain Regarding Treaty Violation 82

(Tokyo) The Foreign Ministry today issued a lengthy statement regarding Britain's protest against the closure of Antung port to seagoing vessels and its request to reopen the Yalu River railway bridge for ship passage. It stated that Britain has absolutely no reason to protest. The Korean government announced on January 31st that the Yalu River railway bridge would no longer be opened for ship passage after March 15th. British Ambassador to Tokyo, Clive, applied in June to continue this convenience, based on a 1910 Japanese government document stating that the construction of the bridge would not interfere with British trade rights in the Antung port with China, as granted by the 1903 Sino-American Treaty. The Foreign Ministry stated that such a treaty has no right to bind a third party, and Japan believes it has no responsibility to maintain the opening of the bridge. Furthermore, the Yalu River seabed has changed, and seagoing vessels can no longer sail to the Sandotu (transliteration) area seven miles below Antung. Therefore, there is no need to open the bridge. Moreover, the bridge has been in existence for twenty years, and the bridge machinery is dilapidated, requiring a large sum of money for repairs. The Korean government's declaration on January 31st was based on economic reasons.

) Reuter's Dispatch, 13th (

American and French Scholars Overthrow Einstein's Theory of Relativity After 200,000 Trials 83

(Paris) According to Le Matin, American and French scholars, after 200,000 trials, have proven that the theory of relativity invented by the great scientist Einstein is actually a fallacy. Einstein's theory is derived from the theory of constant speed of light by the French physicist Michelson (Note: Michelson conducted experiments on the speed of light in a vacuum in 1852-1931, which formed the basis of the theory of relativity). Now, according to the experiments of American and French scholars, Michelson's theory is untenable.

The newspaper concluded, "Since the facts have been proven, Einstein's theory of relativity, which is derived from Michelson's theory, is naturally without foundation." (Havas Dispatch, 12th)

Improvement in Financial Situation of British Colonies 84

(London) Colonial Secretary Sir Philip Cunliffe-Lister stated in the House of Commons today during the debate on the colonial budget that the financial situation of British colonies has improved. He said that a few years ago, many colonies relied on British government assistance. Now, the budget has reached equilibrium. Ceylon has greatly benefited from the rubber and tea industries, which account for three-quarters of its export trade. Malaya's 1932 budget was short by 11 million yuan, but now this number has been reduced to 3 million yuan. (Reuter's Dispatch, 12th)

Severe Labor Strike in San Francisco 86

A General Strike is Expected on Monday, Affecting All Industries and Businesses. San Francisco 15,000 workers are already on strike, and another 30,000 will declare a general strike on Monday. This will completely halt all transportation, industry, and commerce along the Pacific coast. The president of the Central Labor Council, Mervyn Rathborne, now has full power to implement or cancel the general strike. He hinted today that he was prepared to order a general strike. (National Telegraph, 12th)

San Francisco Business in San Francisco is increasingly grinding to a halt, and the momentum of the general strike movement is worsening. Transportation between Oakland and San Francisco was completely cut off this morning. 4,000 workers have joined the strike, and 2,000 boilermakers have also gone on strike, so work in shipyards and railway factories cannot proceed. All dyeing factories have been closed, and slaughterhouses will also cease operations at 6 p.m. on Saturday due to the slaughterhouse union's declaration of a strike. Electrical workers and streetcar repair workers are scheduled to start striking at 10 a.m. this morning. Drivers and ticket sellers must vote again on Sunday to decide. All businesses will be severely affected. Because of the streetcar shutdown, many workers and clerks who work in San Francisco but live in the east will either have to stop working or stay in the city. It is said that the general strike movement is the most severe today since the International Longshoremen's Association declared a strike on May 9th. With the support of workers in various industries, dockworkers and sailors are expected to reject the arbitration proposal of the government mediator, which was accepted by the employers yesterday. A majority of the 129 unions here have approved the general strike, but it depends on the final order of the Central Labor Executive Department. Local labor unions are now trying to avoid the realization of the general strike, but judging from the current situation, it may not succeed unless the employers accept all the workers' conditions. The National Guard is still patrolling the coastal area, which is very quiet today. There have been some disturbances elsewhere, but nothing major. There should be no problem with food after the general strike for the time being. This morning, food merchants claimed that the current stock could support the entire city for a month. ) National Telegraph, 12th (

Inside Story of the Okada Cabinet Formation 87

No Different Than Extending the Life of the Saito Cabinet According to the Tokyo Hochi Shimbun, the sudden emergence of General Keisuke Okada to form a cabinet was truly unexpected by the world. The reason for this actually came from Saito's own intention and was related to the so-called crisis approaching in 1936 and the fundamental policies to address diplomacy and national defense. Okada served as the Minister of the Navy in the Tanaka and Saito cabinets. At the time of the conclusion of the London Naval Treaty, he served as a military councilor, being an intermediate figure mediating between the hardliners (Military Affairs Bureau system) and the treaty faction (Ministry of the Navy system) within the Navy. He was quite confident in overcoming the naval difficulties. However, the young officers regarded him as a treaty faction and were mostly dissatisfied. In fact, he did not lean towards any faction. When the naval treaty was concluded, Navy Minister Takarabe and Plenipotentiary Wakatsuki had already joined forces, making it difficult to break through. The young officers then criticized him as a treaty faction. When Saito was about to resign at the end of June and recommended Okada as his successor, the so-called treaty faction prevented the Chief of the Naval General Staff from making a memorial to the Emperor, but Admiral Suzuki Kantaro, the Chief of Staff, strongly disagreed. Because Suzuki and Okada were relatives—Okada's daughter married Suzuki—the two were quite close. Saito and Okada also had a close relationship as seniors and juniors. This was one personal reason for the recommendation. Secondly, the difficulty of the disarmament conference was imminent. Saito and Suzuki were both naval admirals. If they were too tough, they could not avoid a rupture of the international crisis. Therefore, elder statesmen all valued this. When Saito recommended Okada, Prince Saionji considered it appropriate, and other senior officials had no objections. This was because Okada was rich in compromise. If they wanted to overcome the difficulties of the disarmament conference, they had to resort to compromise. Even if the hardliners and young officers were dissatisfied with him, Okada himself had the magnanimity to deal with it. Moreover, his attitude was very firm. If the young officers made things difficult for him, he would angrily say, "If you do not trust me, please kill me!" This point was well known to Saito. Therefore, Okada's appearance could ease the hardliners within the Navy and break through the international crisis. Moreover, Okada's wealth of compromise had been proven during the Saito cabinet.

He resigned as Minister of the Navy, allowing Osumi to succeed him, and his willingness to live a leisurely life was originally for the reason of stopping disputes. However, even if he wanted to extend his position, it was not impossible, and many people hoped that he would continue to serve, but he refused. Furthermore, the hardliners, such as the anti-treaty faction within the Navy, pursued the Seiyukai for responsibility for violating the treaty. For example, in the temporary parliament of the seventh year, a major crisis occurred between the government and the Seiyukai due to the rice problem. Okada defended Saito and worked hard. Furthermore, when Hatoyama, a cabinet member from the Seiyukai, resigned as Minister of Education, Mori Kaku and Okada's compromise appeased the Seiyukai and allowed the parliament to pass. From these three points of view, Okada was not only rich in compromise but also Saito's mediator. Therefore, Saito deeply admired his ability and persuaded him. Therefore, Okada's cabinet formation was no different than extending the life of the Saito cabinet.

Tianjin Correspondence The newly编战区 special police team of Hebei Province has been waiting in Caicun, Cangxian, to be dispatched to Luan East for two months. In various counties and towns, due to the pervasive atmosphere of drugs, families are ruined and more and more people become bandits. If the green gauze curtains rise, it will be an opportunity for them to gather and rob. Therefore, this matter has no choice but to quietly wait for Huang's return for negotiations. It was recently rumored in Pingfang that China and Japan will convene a meeting in Tianjin on various matters in the war zone, with Tao Shangming, Yin Rugeng, and Shibayama Iga as the central figures of the meeting. Inquiries with the authorities here revealed that there was no such thing. In fact, Shibayama's so-called "Kwantung Army's affair" is by no means a lie, because the number of Japanese troops stationed in the war zone and the number of our current security teams have a deep sense of proportion. If the newly編 special police team of 8,000 people goes there, with newer equipment and stricter discipline, it will not be possible for the currently stationed Japanese troops to monitor them. Therefore, the Japanese side regards this as a very important issue, which cannot be resolved in Tianjin by third- or fourth-rate figures. The authorities feel extremely棘手 about the matter of cracking down on Japanese and Korean ruffians in the war zone. They have repeatedly raised the issue with the Japanese side, saying that condoning the Japanese and Koreans to set up drug institutions everywhere, committing adultery and criminal offenses, and not allowing our local authorities to crack down on them, and blaming us for failing to protect them, is not in line with reason. When we raise this matter, the Japanese verbally express their apologies and say that they will investigate and send them back to their home countries one by one when they have time. However, in practice, no matter how we negotiate, not only is there no crackdown, but after each negotiation, several newly established drug institutions appear in the war zone. The more we hate and value it, the more the Japanese promote and spread it. It is more effective to take a calm attitude and ignore it than to negotiate and protest. ) 11th (

Xu and He Cannot Connect 92

The bandits concentrated their main force to fight back desperately. After more than ten days of fierce fighting, we have made no significant progress. The bandits abandoned important cities and fortresses such as Desheng Mountain, Zhenlong Pass, and Tongjiang and concentrated on the Wanyuan line. Their attempt is tentatively assumed to be: 1. Taking the intermediate route from Chengkou to Wuxi and Fengjie. The view is desolate, the roads are rugged, and often after fifty or sixty li, no human smoke is seen. Outside, it is estimated that the bandits in northern Sichuan will actively flee south and join forces with He's bandits. In fact, the nature of Xu's bandits and He's bandits is very different. Xu's bandits are true communists. He's bandits have very little strength and have become vagrant bandits who only bind and plunder wealthy families everywhere, which is no different from ordinary bandits. If Xu and He intend to join forces, He must gather in the valleys between Shizhu and Lichuan to wait for Xu to flee south. However, He has now deeply fled into the territory of Guizhou, which shows that he does not want to join forces with Xu. 4. Since Xu's bandits' attempt to flee south cannot be realized, those who desperately counterattacked our Fifth Route Army in the Wanyuan area the day before yesterday should be advancing as a retreat, using the momentum of the attack to cover the retreat of the remaining bandits in Tongnan. The most realistic attempt at present is probably still to retreat to the Daba Mountains and take the opportunity to peep at southern Shaanxi."

Bandits Attempt to Hold Firm in One Corner 93

The day before yesterday, Yang Sen of the Fourth Route went to Tongcheng to inspect the results. Yong Shoukang, the head of the regiment of my department, was captured, escaped from Tongjiang, and hid near Tongcheng. The natives treated him extremely well and tried every means to protect him and get him out of danger. Their hatred of the bandits and affection for us can be seen from this. Even when we arrived, the natives expressed extreme friendliness. According to them, the bandits' retreat from Tongjiang was decided as early as March of this year. Therefore, at that time, they began to move the machinery of various factories to Wangping, the rear of Dehan City, and robbed pigs, cattle, sheep, chickens, ducks, stone mills, farm tools, tables, and benches. Even the door bolts were moved and cleaned, and all the houses were burned down. Tongcheng has several salt wells, but the salt production is extremely small. Eighty taels of salt require three thousand firewood wells. After many investigations by my department, the bandits seem to have no intention of disturbing Lower East and western Hubei. The reason why they gathered so many livestock and farm tools is probably to use their 200,000 people to hold firm in one corner, recuperate, and cultivate strength, waiting for the country to have more troubles before coming out to harass again."

(The Attitudes of Britain and America Towards the Naval Disarmament Conference) American Correspondence (America Does Not Abandon its Original Position; Britain Must Maintain Maritime Hegemony) 96

The preparatory meeting for the Naval Disarmament Conference has already begun in London. This meeting naturally has its own unique characteristics. Whether the formal conference next year can succeed depends on this preparatory meeting. It is an important key to future peace in the Pacific. The main countries participating in this meeting—the United States, Britain, and Japan—each have different opinions, and their goals are different. For example, the United States wants to maintain transportation across the two oceans, insists on the doctrine of large ships and big guns, and advocates extending the London Naval Treaty. Britain wants to ensure the security of its maritime colonies around the world, and its navy must be superior to other countries, so it wants to expand its military strength. Japan's dominance in the Far East has become a trend, and it wants to compete with Britain and the United States, so it strongly advocates equality in armaments. These opinions are not merely technical issues; they are the reefs of the preparatory meeting and a huge cancer in the current international situation. We also know that the United States, among the countries in the world today, is relatively unwilling to compete militarily. It also has no immediate plans to use force in the Pacific. However, it has its own special views on the navy and is also making preparations.

Because the current President Franklin Roosevelt served as Undersecretary of the Navy before World War I and after the Washington Conference, he has some goodwill towards Japan, but in reality, he did his best to prepare the navy during his tenure, especially in the military preparation in the Pacific. The construction of fortresses in the Philippines and Guam was due to the excessive cost of engineering facilities in those two places and the long time required, and also because Manila is far from the U.S. naval base (the sea voyage is about 8,000 miles). In any case, the current strength of the United States is difficult to reliably ensure the safety of Manila, so it strives to operate its vanguard base in Pearl Harbor (a seaport belonging to Hawaii) as a fulcrum for the Far East. Recently, there have also been proposals to operate the Aleutian Islands as airfields. This undoubtedly shows that it is paying close attention to the situation in the Far East.

President Roosevelt has a deep relationship with the naval community. Although he does not directly oppose Japan, he is not willing to give in easily. As for the current Secretary of the Navy, Swanson, he is an out-and-out advocate of a strong navy. He is confident that he has the mission of building an invincible U.S. navy in the world, so he has an amazing plan for a large navy. In front of the American people, he shouted that the U.S. Navy has become decayed and cannot be used. He advised the American people to immediately recognize and implement his naval plan, saying, "Our aggressive neighbor to the west is eyeing the Philippines covetously..."

"The future of the great republic lies at sea." The American people already have a considerable understanding of this, and they feel that the international status of the United States would be very dangerous without a strong navy, so he also advocated that "the 5:5:3 ratio is absolutely fair and appropriate and should be permanently continued." There are also authoritative officers in naval warfare, such as Admiral Pratt, who expressed his views on international naval relations, opposing Japan's claim to naval equality. He believes that Japan does not need a navy like Britain to guard the world's oceans. Japan is not like the United States, which is located between the Atlantic, Pacific, and South Seas. Once a war breaks out, Japan's neutral status and its responsibilities are not as great as those of Britain and the United States. Even if there is a war, other countries cannot impose military or economic blockades on Japan. Furthermore, increasing the ratio would be difficult to bear, considering Japan's national treasury revenue. Such arguments are enough to strengthen the U.S. authorities' opinions on naval disarmament and more clearly tend to extend the past naval treaties and maintain the old ratio, causing future disputes.

Such is the atmosphere in North America. Looking out across the Atlantic, what will Britain, which has long occupied the maritime throne, do? Britain's navy cannot be represented by the Naval Ministry, let alone the current Secretary of the Navy, Monsell, who is a retired naval commander. However, Monsell served as Undersecretary of the Navy when the construction of the Singapore naval base was being fiercely debated in the House of Commons, and he made various effective activities. He said, "The mission of the British Navy is not only to protect the British coast but also to maintain the safety of our country's overseas trade. In other words, it is to protect maritime transportation routes. After the Washington Conference, the defense of Hong Kong was agreed to be maintained as it is, while the construction of the Singapore port is absolutely necessary to defend navigation." This shows Britain's true intentions. This kind of thinking has not changed to this day. To make it the world's number one naval power, Britain's tone of expanding its navy, even if it has not been sung as high as the United States, but the actual preparation work has not been relaxed in the slightest. (June 10, Washington)

The Vanguard of the Southern Route Army Approaches Yudu丨Ye Jianying's Troops Suffer Heavy Losses in Zhandang丨Guangzhou Correspondence 97

On the 29th, they arrived at Ouyang Jiang's department and asked to be brought to surrender. Currently, the 4th and 6th companies of the 2nd Battalion of the Pseudo 66th Regiment and local guerrillas of about 300 people are stationed in Zhongcun. The Ping City Council Responds to the Municipal Government's Budget Estimate 98

Ping News, The Ping City Council recently responded to the municipal government regarding the local budget estimate for the 23rd year, saying, "1. We have received the notification from your government regarding the review and revision of the budget estimate for the 23rd year, requesting reconsideration, etc. It was submitted for discussion at the 24th regular meeting of the second phase on the 4th of this month. It was generally believed that although the income and expenditure of the budget for the 23rd year are still suitable, the expenses for salaries and consumption are high, and the expenses for construction projects are low. The salary item listed by the municipal government is more than 9,600 yuan higher than that of the 22nd year, and the consumption is more than 6,300 yuan higher, without explanation, which is inconsistent with the mayor's usual declaration of "one person's meal for two people, two people's work for one person." Furthermore, the staff of various agencies have not been appointed according to law, and their salaries have not been paid according to law. The mayor alone receives a special office fee of up to 1,000 yuan per month in addition to his salary. The celebration fee is 3,600 yuan per year. During the national crisis, the central government has repeatedly ordered to simplify it, so there is no need to continue the previous extravagance. Moreover, it is only a celebration of the official office, and various legal entities have not been invited, so there is no need for such a large expense. The entertainment fee is 4,800 yuan per year. Although Beijing has diplomatic relations, there are the Executive Yuan's Political Reorganization Committee stationed in Beijing and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Custody Office stationed in Beijing. The municipal government only represents this city and does not need such a large expense. In May of this year, during the heavy national humiliation commemoration, a garden party was held at a cost of several thousand yuan, and Yenching University girls were appointed to practice hospitality, which has already been greatly regretted by the people. All of the above points should be reduced. This council understands that the initial budget estimate was proposed, and many things have been followed, so it will be lenient and not delve into it, in order to gradually get on track. Unexpectedly, it is still not enough to meet the mayor's wishes, which is difficult for the city council. The reasons for the review are that the supervision of autonomy is the original right of the mayor. The autonomous elections of the districts and neighborhoods of this city have already been completed. The mayor supervises according to law and allocates the existing staff of the municipal government according to their capabilities, which can be sufficient. There is no need to set up additional sections and shares, and there is no need for such a huge amount of more than 30,000 yuan per year. Moreover, since autonomy is set as the beginning period, preparing for the completion of autonomy is the responsibility of the city council, and there is no need to set up an autonomous supervision office. The vehicle donation is a major source of revenue for this city. The revised regulations on vehicle donation in this city do not have any provisions for exemption. It is heard that the vehicles of Chairman Huang of the Executive Yuan's Political Reorganization Committee stationed in Beijing have all been donated, and the same is true for others. There are records for business operations, and taxes and donations have never been heard of. The mayor has always claimed to be unafraid of boundaries and resistance, and his resistance to donating may be an excuse to avoid it. It concerns annual income and he must be able to find a way to collect it, so that there is no loss. As for bicycles, they are the most popular product, with a trend of traveling thousands of miles a day. There are registration of more than 75,000 vehicles with names and addresses that can be checked. According to the regulations, each vehicle should donate two yuan per year, amounting to more than 100,000 yuan. How can we allow omissions and not donate? Even if there are losses from resale, the number must not be large. Instead of being harsh and bitter to the small people, it is more fair to collect donations according to law. If we abandon this plan, and lightly defend this huge amount of omissions, the members who collect it will inevitably be derelict in their duties. This council believes that the revenue from vehicle donations is more than this number. Although there has been an increase in education and roads in the business sector, the funds for health are still not evenly developed. Moreover, the roads in the suburbs are related to transportation, rural education, and the people's livelihood. The equipment for science experiments in middle schools is incomplete, resulting in the worst graduation performance. The river channels and ditches are not repaired, which is detrimental to hygiene and cleanliness, so they are added in amount. In short, deciding on budgets and final accounts is the special right of the people's representatives and the important responsibility that the people's representatives should bear for the people. They have the right to review and the right to amend. Although the political systems of various countries are different, and the measures are different, the budgets submitted to the parliament are always amended before they are passed. The budget estimate for this city in the 23rd year should have been submitted earlier, but it was delayed and not sent. It was repeatedly urged and sent on April 28th of this year, close to the central review period. It is heard that the municipal government sent the previous budget to the council and also sent it to the central government, hoping to be approved directly. The councilors were deeply horrified. The review of the second-level budget by this council has been approved by the Executive Yuan according to law and ordered to be complied with. It has been reviewed and sent to the central government first, which is a violation of laws and regulations. If it is not necessary to be decided by this council and can be approved, then the right of decision of the city council stipulated by laws and regulations is a mere formality. The responsibility for such out-of-bounds behavior should be borne by the mayor. As for the budget notification of this council for the 23rd year, the municipal government did not consult with it and immediately reduced it. The expenses of this council were originally provisional, and the budget changes from year to year. The salaries and consumption of the municipal government can be increased without reason, while this council has too little funds, and there are various omissions in travel expenses, entertainment printing, stoves, etc., and the facts are difficult. The amount has been increased and has been reported to the Executive Yuan. Moreover, during this review, the speaker and deputy speaker repeatedly consulted with the mayor, who agreed to do so. The notification turned the previous discussion upside down, which also hinders credibility. The budget for the 23rd year has now entered the beginning period. Since it has been revised and passed, it is not convenient to change it again. The members of the council unanimously voted to specially inspect the original documents and respond to the investigation. This notification is for the Beijing Municipal Government."

Zhejiang Construction Department Develops Aquatic Products Industry Formulates Six Measures 100

Quzhou Correspondence Zhejiang Province faces the sea to the east, with numerous islands and a coastline of more than 1,300 li. The rivers include the Qiantang River in the north, the Jiao River and Ou River in the middle, and the Feiyun River and Ao River in the south. Other lakes, marshes, rivers, and streams are also scattered like stars. The vastness of the fishing grounds and the richness of the water resources are the best in the southeast. The value of the annual fishery products along the coast and rivers in Zhejiang Province is estimated to be about 8 million yuan for Ningbo, about 600,000 yuan for Zhapu, about 3 million yuan for Shipu, about 3 million yuan for Shaoxing, about 2 million yuan for Zhenhai, and about 10 million yuan for Wenzhou and Taizhou combined. Together with Jiangsu Province, it is more than 60 million yuan per year. The reproduction of fish is no less than that of Japan, but in recent years, the domestic demand is not enough, and it still needs to be supplied by Japan, Hong Kong, Macau, and other places. The total value of aquatic products imported from foreign countries each year averages more than 30 million yuan. Zhejiang Province's fish production has suffered from Japanese cross-border fishing and low-price dumping to us, and the business is declining day by day and life is becoming increasingly difficult. The Construction Department is aware of this, and believes that if the fisheries in the province are declining and no urgent measures are taken to provide relief, not only will the development of fisheries be hopeless, but hundreds of thousands of fishermen in Zhejiang Province will be bankrupt. It has decided to immediately find ways to provide relief, starting with protecting fisheries and regulating the fishermen's economy, and has formulated six measures to develop fisheries as follows: (1) Instruct the offshore water police to effectively maintain the security of the fishing grounds. Each coastal county, or a combination of several counties, may also set up ocean-going ships equipped with weapons for patrol and guard during the fishing season. (2) Issue fishery public bonds or raise funds to establish a fishery bank and loan office in the fishing area, and at the same time urge fishermen to organize marketing and other various cooperatives. (3) Establish a training institute for fishery guidance personnel. After graduation, they will be assigned to fishing areas to teach fishermen the necessary knowledge and skills in fisheries. At the same time, establish fishery guidance offices in important fishing areas to solve the fishermen's difficulties at any time. (4) Promote new organizations in fisheries, purchase new fishing vessels and fishing gear, and plan to establish fishing gear manufacturing plants and scientific manufacturing plants for aquatic products. (5) Set up refrigerated transport ships and weather observation stations. (6) Establish large-scale fish and shellfish breeding grounds along the coast and in areas with large lakes and marshes, and set up breeding farms. (5th)

Wang Tongsi, a farmer in Yangliyan Bridge, fourth district, was extremely anxious because his rice seedlings were withered. He asked people to scoop water to irrigate his fields, which cost one yuan and five cents per mu each time, and he wanted to make a prior agreement. Wang was a poor man, and when he saw this situation, he was worried and committed suicide by hanging himself. By the time his family discovered it, it was too late to save him. It was also very tragic. Rice prices have reached eleven yuan and several cents due to the lack of supply due to the small amount of water, and unscrupulous merchants are hoarding and speculating. Actively Planning for Drought Relief 111

Since the 28th of last month, the weather has been hot and humid, with no rain, and signs of disaster have emerged, causing rice prices to soar. White rice is now ten yuan and eight jiao per dan. In the past two days, the heat has increased further, reaching 102 degrees indoors and 110 degrees outdoors. At 4:00 PM on the 12th, dark clouds gathered, and a thunderstorm occurred, lasting only about a quarter of an hour. Only half an inch of rain fell, and the farmland in the surrounding countryside has no water for irrigation. The drinking water supply has been cut off, causing great panic among the residents. The river channels in the urban area are so dry that the bottom can be seen, causing difficulties for transportation, drinking water, and fire fighting. The latrines in various places are full of waste because the boats transporting manure from the countryside cannot come to the city, causing the waste to flow into the streets, which has a significant impact on sanitation. The supply of firewood and straw has also been cut off. In view of this, the local New Life Movement Promotion Association plans to find ways to remedy the situation. A meeting was specifically convened yesterday, and the following resolutions were made: 1. Build dams at all the water gates of the four city gates, and use electricity at the West Water Gate to pump water from the Liangxi River into the city. 2. The association will submit the plan to the First District Office for implementation within three days. 3. The project requires 800 yuan. The association will first donate 50 yuan to show its support. The remaining amount will be allocated to the District Office and the town offices in the city. 4. For electricity, please contact the Qishuyan Power Plant to offer the lowest price and fulfill its obligations. District Chief Qian will go to make contact. 5.

The First District Office convened an emergency meeting of the town leaders in the city to discuss the implementation methods. As for Director of the Construction Bureau Zhang Fulin, in order to plan the dredging of important waterways to the Yangtze River, he specially accompanied Technical Section Chief Huang Dechun to Cheng to consult with Cheng County Magistrate Bao on opening the Huangtiangang Sluice to introduce the Yangtze River water into the inland river to facilitate traffic between Wuxi and Cheng. Regarding the issue of opening the Dongba Dam requested by the officials and people of Wujin, neighboring counties unanimously opposed it. Yesterday, the Wuxi and Yixing public legal groups jointly submitted a petition to the provincial authorities, emphasizing the advantages and disadvantages of the Dongba Dam and requesting a stern rejection. At the same time, the entrances to the Yangtze River and the major inland rivers in Wujin, Jiangyin, Changshu, and other places should be promptly inspected, and dredging should be selectively carried out to facilitate water flow and irrigate farmland. At the same time, the Wuxi Chamber of Commerce also sent letters to the relevant counties regarding the Dongba Dam issue, requesting unanimous support. The Wujin County Magistrate Cai Pei, together with Gao Zhenbai, the Party Committee member of the county, went to the provincial government to seek instructions and have already returned to Changzhou. The provincial government also advocates caution and has decided not to open the Dongba Dam and to seek other ways to connect to the Yangtze River for drought relief. In addition, Sha Yankai, a famous lawyer from Yixing, also sent a letter to Qian Sunqing in this city, detailing the history of the Dongba Dam and stating that there is no reason to open it.

The Provincial Government of Changzhou Does Not Intend to Open the Dongba Dam 113

Wujin County is experiencing a drought with no rain, and signs of disaster have emerged. The county government has specifically established a disaster prevention committee to plan relief measures. After discussion, it was decided to request the provincial government to approve the opening of the Dongba Dam to relieve the immediate crisis. County Magistrate Cai Ziping and Gao Bozhen, the representative of the County Party Department, went to the provincial government on the 11th to petition. They have now returned to Changzhou. According to County Magistrate Cai, after Yixing County requested the opening of the Dongba Dam, the provincial government sent personnel to inspect the Dongba Dam. As a result, the water level of the Dongba Dam was one foot lower than in previous years. If the dam is opened widely, the floodwaters will inundate the area, causing great danger. It will cost two to three million to rebuild the dam in the future. Where will such a large amount of money come from? If the dam is opened slightly, only Liyang County will benefit, and other counties will not receive any benefit. Therefore, it is advisable not to open the Dongba Dam. Subsequently, County Magistrate Cai offered the following suggestions since the Dongba Dam could not be opened: 1. Pump the water from the rivers and lakes into the inland rivers. 2. Pump the water from the inland rivers into the tributaries. 3. Pump the water from the tributaries to irrigate farmland. This plan was adopted by the provincial government.

Villagers in Yangzhou Open Fire and Mistakenly Kill a Police Officer 116

The fourth squad of the second company of the Jiangdu County Security Team was stationed in Huaiziqiao Town. He immediately led the team to rush to rescue. However, as soon as they left the town by 100 meters, a bullet came flying towards them and hit Zhang Kaicheng, a first-class soldier, in the head. The squad leader has already come to the city overnight to report to the county security team headquarters, which dispatched Deputy Squad Leader Zhao Qingshi to rush to investigate on the morning of the 12th. Tang Zhengyi and others also admitted to opening fire without denying it. It was also found that the origin of the voices and gongs was that Chen Sanlai, a fisherman, was holding a ceremony with shamans to pray for blessings because his daughter-in-law had died and his wife was ill. Many people watched, causing the police team to mistakenly believe it was a bandit robbery. Wenzhuang also heard the sound of voices and gongs, followed by gunfire, resulting in one mistake leading to another and causing a fatality.

Farmer in Hangzhou Commits Suicide Due to Economic Pressure 118

Zhang Acai, a farmer from Zhongbuqiao in Hang County, who was nearly thirty years old, was usually diligent and thrifty, law-abiding and content. Recently, due to the sharp drop in silk prices and the low value of grain hurting farmers, the income from his hard work was not enough to cover the costs. His mother, daughter, wife, and children had no means of support, leading to a growing mountain of debt and accumulated arrears. Although he went out to make arrangements everywhere, he could not find a solution. He then conceived the idea of committing suicide to escape from the sea of suffering. He hanged himself on a beam yesterday. By the time it was discovered, he had already died.

Fire on Jiaoren Road 119

The Yuechangsheng Southern Goods Store at No. 181 Jiaoren Road, Hangzhou, caught fire at 3:15 AM yesterday (the 13th) due to a careless mosquito candle. In an instant, the fierce flames soared. Fortunately, the fire brigades of the fire departments arrived one after another and worked hard to put out the fire, which was extinguished after an hour of burning. A total of eight shops were burned, including the Juleyuan Teahouse, the Wang Yonghe Hotel, and the Shenchangxiang Mill, with losses estimated at more than 10,000 yuan. Mao Juyuan, an 82-year-old man who lived in the Shunchangxiang, was unable to escape and was buried in the fire. The shop owner's wife and son, Lian Sheng, were also injured and sent to the hospital for treatment.

Local News

Amidst the Intense Heat, Officials and People of This City Unanimously Prevent Drought; City Government Purchases a Large Number of Water Lifting Machines; Farmers Petition for Assistance 120

According to the Central News Agency, the sun has been scorching and the weather has been intensely hot for days, and agricultural products are withering due to the impact of the severe drought. Various sectors are actively seeking ways to remedy the situation. Various charitable organizations began setting up altars to pray for rain yesterday. The city government has specifically allocated funds to purchase water lifting machines, and the Municipal Farmers' Association will also assist the government in drought relief efforts. The details are as follows:

Municipal Affairs Meeting 121

The Social Affairs Bureau received a petition from the farmers' associations in various districts, stating that there had been no rain for a long time and that a drought was about to occur. It was requested that water lifting machines be purchased as soon as possible to relieve the agricultural production. The bureau drafted a plan and submitted it to the city government, requesting an allocation of 5,000 yuan to purchase water lifting machines. The city government held a municipal affairs meeting yesterday, attended by all bureau chiefs, chaired by Mayor Wu. In addition to discussing other cases, the purchase of water lifting machines to relieve agricultural production was passed and handed over to the Social Affairs Bureau for management.

Mayor's Remarks 122

A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Mayor Wu yesterday to inquire about the drought prevention issue in this city. He kindly made the following remarks: Since the beginning of summer, there has been little rainfall and the weather has been hot, which has not been seen in decades. The rivers and lakes are gradually drying up. In the areas near the rivers, there is still water that can be lifted, while the areas farther away from the rivers are showing signs of drought. If we do not urgently seek relief, there is no hope for the autumn harvest, and there will be food shortages. There are two ways to provide relief: addressing the root cause and addressing the symptoms. Measures such as opening and dredging rivers, digging artesian wells, and organizing farmers' cooperatives to provide credit loans are all fundamental solutions. However, in the face of a severe drought, these measures are too slow to be effective. Therefore, we have to consider addressing the symptoms. What the farmers in this city want and urgently need now is a sufficient supply of water. At this moment, most of the rivers in the urban areas are dry. For the time being, we can only find ways to divert water from the main rivers into the tributaries, and then farmers can draw water from the tributaries to irrigate their fields. Therefore, at the municipal affairs meeting yesterday morning, we discussed emergency relief measures and agreed that we should first purchase a large number of water lifting machines and distribute them to various districts, and send engineers to guide the diversion of water and the construction of dams. We should carefully plan relief measures according to the special circumstances of each district. We know that the city treasury is extremely tight, but this matter concerns the people's food, so we have to reluctantly provide support. We decided to proceed as planned and immediately handed it over to the Social Affairs Bureau, together with the Finance, Land, and Public Security Bureaus, to proceed as quickly as possible to relieve the people's plight and satisfy the farmers' expectations. The fundamental solutions should still be planned as soon as possible, so we have also ordered the competent authorities to carefully discuss the methods and implement them step by step.

Public Announcement of Machine Purchase 123

The Social Affairs Bureau issued a public announcement yesterday, stating that since the beginning of summer this year, there has been little rainfall and the weather has been hot and severely dry. The rice seedlings in the farmland are gradually withering. In addition to sending personnel to various districts and towns to inspect the disaster situation, the bureau intends to purchase water lifting machines for relief purposes to avoid affecting the agricultural harvest. If you have pumps ranging from six to twelve horsepower, please provide details of the following items: 1. How much water is discharged per hour? 2. What kind of oil is used for the engine? 3. What is the value? Please come to the bureau to discuss this today (the 14th) from 9:00 AM to 4:00 PM so that we can make purchases. This is hereby announced.

Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, dozens of representatives from the Municipal Farmers' Association and various district farmers' associations departed from the North Station and went to the city's central district to petition the city government. At this time, the city government was holding a municipal affairs meeting and had already discussed the drought prevention issue in detail, deciding to allocate funds to purchase a large number of water lifting machines and distribute them to various rural districts for application. Mayor Wu then sent Wu Huanru, the second section chief of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, to receive them on his behalf. Yu Zhenhui, a standing committee member of the Municipal Farmers' Association, stated their intention. Section Chief Wu then relayed the discussion of the municipal affairs meeting to the representatives and hoped that the representatives could assist the government in drought prevention efforts. The representatives were satisfied and left. According to Section Chief Wu, who spoke to reporters after the representatives left, the government has decided to allocate funds to purchase a large number of water lifting machines and distribute them to various rural districts. Starting tomorrow (i.e., today), a public announcement will be published, and those who need water lifting machines can register. The bureau will also send personnel to inspect and arrange the location of the water lifting machines and how to build dams. All procedures are now being expedited to meet the urgent need. The Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have been without rain since the beginning of summer. During the plum season, the weather is hot and dry, like a scorching summer. The rural areas of our country have been bankrupt in recent years, and everything on the market is declining day by day. If another disaster occurs and this ray of hope is extinguished, the social situation will be truly precarious. We are worried about: First, in recent years, there have been repeated disasters of war, floods, and droughts in various provinces, and all rely on Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces to find ways to provide relief. If Jiangsu and Zhejiang also suffer a disaster, who will help? We will have to wait to die with our hands tied. We are worried about: Second, recently, the interior provinces have been filled with party bandits, half of whom are forced by hunger and cold. If a disaster occurs, like sparrows driven by a flock of birds, the good and weak people will also take risks. The example of the roving bandits of the late Ming Dynasty can serve as a warning. We are worried about: Third, diseases are rampant and deaths are increasing daily. If it does not rain again, the heat will continue to rise, and it will inevitably lead to a great epidemic that cannot be saved. We are worried about: Fourth, the signs of Heaven are actually transferred by human affairs. In the past, government offices often prayed to the gods and prohibited slaughter during floods and droughts. Heaven and man responded, and every request was answered. Christians are already praying for rain. Therefore, we respectfully request the government to cherish the people as if they were injured, embody Heaven's virtue of loving life, hold prayer for rain and ban slaughter to advocate this, and at the same time, issue an order to all counties and subordinates to sincerely observe it. With the spirit inspired, there is hope that sweet rain will fall immediately. The matter is urgent, and the way is in sincerity. Please quickly implement it. The benefits will be unimaginable." Sun Enjun Arrives in Shanghai to Discuss Cotton Matters 138

A banking syndicate is forming to develop cotton production in the Northwest. Mr. Sun Enjun, member of the National Economic Council's Cotton Industry Control Committee and director of the Central Cotton Improvement Institute, visited the provinces of Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, and Shaanxi last month to investigate and implement measures related to cotton production in the Northwest and to handle the affairs of cotton production and sales cooperatives. He has now completed his official duties and arrived in Shanghai yesterday by boat from Nantong. According to Mr. Sun, the rainfall in the Northwest this year has been favorable, resulting in a better agricultural harvest compared to previous years, especially for cotton. The Cotton Industry Control Committee is currently establishing large-scale cotton production and sales cooperatives in the Shaanxi and Henan areas and is introducing Shanghai banks to invest in them. The loans for these cooperatives are divided into three categories: 1) cotton harvesting, 2) ginning, and 3) credit cooperation. The total investment required is approximately two million yuan, with the first category accounting for the majority. The second and third categories account for only 15%, approximately 300,000 yuan. Banks such as Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, National Industrial Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and Jin Cheng Bank have already formed a cotton production and sales cooperative investment banking syndicate to share the investment amounts. Except for the Bank of China, which still needs to be contacted, the rest have already signed contracts.

Page 13

Implementing the Reorganization of Brokerage Tax, Prohibiting Forced Solicitation of Customers and Goods, and Restricting the Collection of Commissions: The Ministry of Finance Issues Seven Directives for Compliance 144

According to the Xinxin News Agency, the Ministry of Finance believes that the brokerage tax in various provinces and cities is rife with abuses. At the recent National Financial Conference, it was resolved to reorganize the brokerage tax with seven measures. Yesterday, it specifically informed various provinces and cities to instruct the financial departments to comply with the measures. The directive has already arrived in Shanghai, and its measures are excerpted as follows: 1) Limiting Brokerage Firms: Brokerage firms must have fixed business locations in county, city, town, and market trading locations to obtain a license to operate, regardless of short or long term. 2) Defining Brokerage Firm Responsibilities: Brokerage firms are the key intermediaries for goods transactions and must not operate privately without a license or use one license for multiple purposes, nor should they engage in forced solicitation of customers and goods that resemble monopolies. 3) Restricting Brokerage Commissions: Brokerage firms' commission rates vary greatly across provinces and cities, ranging from about 7% to 5%. Given the current difficulties faced by farmers and businesses and the low prices, it seems appropriate to restrict them. It is proposed to set the limit at 3%, with each province and city considering local trading conditions and determining the restriction accordingly. 4) Brokerage Business Tax: The standard for brokerage taxation should be based on the amount of sales and commissions. The standard for brokerage taxation varies across provinces, which inevitably leads to uneven burdens. When opening a brokerage firm, fees should be paid and a license obtained in accordance with regulations. The annual brokerage business tax should be based on the amount of sales, and the provincial finance departments should formulate measures based on the old system, refer to the current situation, and submit them to the Ministry of Finance for approval. If the tax is collected based on the amount of sales, the tax rate must not exceed 3%. If it is based on commissions, the tax rate must not exceed 20%. 5) Wandering Brokerage Tax Should Be Abolished: The nature of brokerage firms varies across provinces and cities. Some brokers and their associates operate in the open air without fixed business locations, despite having licenses and collecting commissions. They arbitrarily collect brokerage fees and cause illegal disturbances, which should be gradually abolished. Fixed business locations should be established to comply with regulations. The steps for abolition should be determined by each province and city, but must be approved by the Ministry of Finance. 6) Correcting Illegal and Excessive Collection Practices: Most provinces and cities comply with regulations regarding brokerage tax, but there are occasional violations, such as setting up checkpoints at trading markets to collect taxes or having merchants bid for contracts, which are burdensome. These practices should be quickly reformed to ensure that tax revenue and commercial conditions are considered together. Bad habits should be gradually abolished after the contract period expires, based on the circumstances. 7) Brokerage Firm Operating Regulations Should Be Specified: When establishing a brokerage firm, guarantees must be provided. The trading methods of brokerage firms vary across provinces, leading to many abuses. For thorough reform, provinces and cities should be required to formulate regulations based on local conditions and submit them to the Ministry for approval. Brokerage firms are responsible for local transactions, and strict regulation is necessary. In particular, consolidation should be prioritized to avoid complexity. When establishing a brokerage firm, guarantees must be provided. If the firm operates legally after establishment, the government should also provide protection. Provinces and cities should formulate appropriate regulations based on local conditions and submit them to the Ministry for approval.

Nahmmacher's Funeral Held Yesterday Morning After His Death 145

Mr. Nahmmacher, Far East Manager of the American United Aviation Machine Trading Company, died in an accident on the afternoon of the day before yesterday when test-flying his recently arrived plane at Hongqiao Airport. His assistant, Mr. Welch, was fortunate to escape. The details of the incident were reported in yesterday's newspaper. The latest news obtained yesterday is reported as follows.

Mr. Nahmmacher's Cremation Yesterday Morning (Carl A. 146

Nahmmacher) When he crashed to his death the day before yesterday, his wife and friends on the scene were unable to provide assistance. Westerners playing golf at the nearby Country Club witnessed the situation and rushed to rescue him, but Mr. Nahmmacher was unable to jump out and died with the plane. The airport authorities then arranged for a vehicle to transport Mr. Nahmmacher's body to the International Funeral Home on Jiaozhou Road for temporary storage. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, the body was transported to the church on Jing'an Temple Road, where Pastor Dr. Threlkeld performed the cremation ceremony. The ceremony was quite simple. Mr. Nahmmacher's body, except for his left hand, which was still similar to its original state, was covered in blood and gore, making it a gruesome sight.

Consulate Condolences 147

Mrs. Nahmmacher was on the scene with her four-year-old son when Mr. Nahmmacher had the accident. When Mr. Nahmmacher crashed from the air, Mrs. Nahmmacher rushed to rescue him, but she was too far away from the crash site. Mrs. Nahmmacher was shocked and anxious and fainted on the way. She was rescued by friends and returned home. By the evening before last, she had recovered. The US Consulate General in Shanghai sent Vice-Consul Lanuo and his wife to visit Mrs. Nahmmacher and to prevent any unforeseen circumstances, they accompanied her all day. Lanuo was also a close friend of Mr. Nahmmacher and a skilled pilot.

Aerial Memorial 148

Mr. Welch, the assistant who survived the accident with Mr. Nahmmacher, luckily landed with a parachute and suffered only minor injuries. Yesterday morning at 5:45 AM, Welch went to Hongqiao Airport to mourn Mr. Nahmmacher's tragic death. He flew a plane alone, circling the crash site and the sky above it several times to express his condolences.

Mr. Welch Speaks About the Accident 149

Mr. Welch said that when the plane was ascending, the speed reached 310 miles per hour, and there was no danger. When descending, the engine should be stopped as usual. However, in mid-air, the plane suddenly shook violently. He knew he was in danger and believed that the wing had fallen off. He jumped out with a parachute at only 400 feet above the ground. Fortunately, he landed in a small river and suffered only minor injuries. If he had landed on land, even if he had not died, he would have been seriously injured because he was too close to the ground.

Telegram Discusses Aftermath 150

After Mr. Nahmmacher's death, the affairs of the United Aviation Machine Trading Company in Shanghai were lacking a person in charge. In order to take care of Mr. Nahmmacher's affairs, the company at 205 Hamilton Building took a temporary vacation from yesterday and urgently telegraphed Mr. Luo Yisi, the company's Deputy Far East Manager in the United States, urging him to return to Shanghai immediately to take charge of everything, as Mr. Luo had just returned to the United States for inspection.

Mr. Nahmmacher's Brief Biography 151

Mr. Nahmmacher was born in Brooklyn, USA, in 1899. He came to China in 1919 and married Mrs. Nahmmacher. They had been married for 11 years and had one son, who was four years old. Mr. Nahmmacher's business in Shanghai, the Xin Guang Automobile Company on Foch Road, was also founded by Mr. Nahmmacher. The United Airlines Company was established in March of last year, and the company's Kessel aircraft business was doing well. Mr. Nahmmacher started flying during the European War, and his skills were extremely refined. In the Far East, he was considered a first-class talent in the aviation industry, with 2,000 hours of flight experience. He was also the first person in China to obtain an aviation license. His death is deeply regretted by all parties.

First Announcement on Cholera Prevention: First Document from the Temporary Office 154

According to the Guowen News Agency, the Shanghai Temporary Cholera Prevention Office issued its first announcement yesterday: 1) Although no true cholera cases have been found in Shanghai this summer, the weather is extremely dry and the heat is very high. The temperature reached 104.4 degrees on the 12th of this month, breaking the local observatory's historical record. Only 1894 was hotter, but it only reached 102.9 degrees. The current extreme heat started on June 25th, when the temperature was 101.5 degrees and the relative humidity was 76.9. Except for June 29th and July 5th, 6th, 7th, 8th, and 9th, the temperature gradually increased thereafter, reaching 104.4 degrees on the 12th. The average relative humidity on July 1st was 67.7, with the highest being 9.5 on June 30th. There was no rain during this period, only two thunderstorms. There was a slight rain on the 18th, measuring 0.02 inches. The drought this year is already a cause for concern. 2) One cholera case was found in Guangzhou on June 9th, two cases were found in Hankou on July 4th, and one case was found in Manila on July 6th. No cases have been found in Shanghai. 3) Due to the extreme heat, many citizens have suffered from heatstroke and have been treated in hospitals. The Xizang Road Epidemic Hospital treated a Chinese patient whose temperature reached 108.4 degrees and whose pulse was 146, but the patient did not die. Most patients suffer from gastrointestinal diseases, diarrhea, and typhoid fever. 4) With the consultation of Mayor Wu and the health authorities of the concessions, the local water company is, as in previous years, providing free tap water to the poor. Tap water faucets are installed on the streets. Nanshi and Zhabei each receive 1 million gallons of free water per month. If this amount is exceeded, the municipal government will subsidize the cost at a rate of 30 cents per thousand gallons. This is because cholera prevention is closely related to the cleanliness of drinking water. 5) In addition, the health authorities of the concessions and Shanghai are working hard to implement prevention methods such as publicity lectures, distributing leaflets, posting slogans, and free injections to achieve the desired preventive effect. 6) As of the end of June, the number of people who have received anti-cholera injections is as follows: Shanghai 164,279 people, Public Concession 96,081 people, French Concession 45,079 people, Railway Bureau Health Section 5,403 people, totaling 310,842 people. 7) Individuals can avoid cholera by paying attention to hygiene. Drinking water must be clean. Cold drinks and ice cream must be purchased from reliable manufacturers. Fresh fruits must be washed with boiling water. Attention must be paid to the utensils used to avoid contamination by servants. Raw vegetables and uncooked foods are best avoided. Each household should ensure that its servants receive free preventive injections. 8) The first meeting of the year was held on April 24th, chaired by Director of the Health Department Liu Ruiheng. The Epidemiology Group held three meetings, and the Publicity Group held two meetings. One point that should be noted is that cholera vibrio with weak agglutination was found three times in the river and pond water samples taken in May and June. This point is important for the study of cholera epidemics. 9) As in previous years, various epidemic hospitals have opened to accommodate patients. The following hospitals have a total of 1,000 beds: Xizang Road Epidemic Hospital, Shanghai Emergency Epidemic Hospital, Public Works Bureau Isolation Hospital, Nanshi Public Hospital, Tangshan Road Hongkou Epidemic Hospital, Nanshi Society Epidemic Hospital, Nanshi Shenzhou Hospital, and Hongkou Civilian Hospital.
